Manichaean Dualism and Its Refutation
Maturidi presents and then refutes the Manichaean dualistic theory.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Manichaean dualistic cosmology of light and darkness and how Imam Maturidi refutes it by exposing its internal contradictions, particularly regarding infinity and finitude.

Core Idea
Every false doctrine contains its own refutation if examined carefully.

Imam Maturidi presents the Manichaean belief in two eternal principles—light and darkness—and their mixture that produces the world. However, as he shows, their own account is so contradictory that it collapses under its own weight. This lesson walks through their cosmology and then the simple, powerful critique Maturidi offers.

Guided Path
1
Read the Manichaean claim
Read the opening part where Maturidi describes their view: two separate principles, light infinite in four directions, darkness infinite below but finite at contact, then mixture.
Notice the claim that darkness attacks light.
2
Understand the details
Note the five colors, five senses, and the spirit Hamama. See how they assign good to light and evil to darkness.
The system is elaborate but has logical problems.
3
Identify the contradiction
Maturidi points out that they say the principles are infinite in some directions but finite in one. This is contradictory because finitude implies a limit, which indicates temporality and dependence.
The phrase 'تفسيره' means explaining it is enough to refute it.
4
Reflect on the method
Maturidi uses the principle that a finite part cannot make an infinite whole. He also shows that if they were infinite from all sides, they would be fully mixed, contradicting the claim of mixture from one side only.
This approach is typical of kalam: using internal logical inconsistencies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة
في صفة أقاويل الثنوية
أقاويل المنانية وبيان فسادها
قال الشيخ رحمه الله : زعمت المنانية أن الأشياء كائنة على ما عليه من امتزاج النور والظلمة. وكانا متباينين: النور في العلو لا يتناهى في أربع جهات شمال وجنوب وصبا ودبور، والظلمة في الشفل كذلك، ولها من جهة الالتقاء تناه فبغت الظلمة على النور فامتزجا، فكان العالم من امتزاجهما على قدر الامتزاج ولكل واحد منهما خمسة أجناس : حمرة وبياض وصفرة وسواد وخضرة. فكل شيء مما جاء من هذا الجنس من جوهر النور فهو خير، وما كان من جوهر الظلمة فهو شر . وكذلك لكل واحد منهما حواس خمس: سمع وبصر وذائق وحاسة الشم واللمس فما أدرك جوهر النور بها فهو خير، وما أدرك جوهر الظلمة الظلمة فهو شر. وللنور روح وللظلمة روح وروح يسمى همامة، وهي حية، فغلب العالم ليحبس النور فيها . والنور ليس بحساس، وما كان منه يكون بالطبع ويكون خيرا كله؛ والهامة حساسة. وسيصير كل واحد منهما إلى حيزه . ثم وجد أعلى الأشياء أصفاها، وأسفلها أكدرها؛ ومن طبعهما الخفة والثقل . وأمرهما على التنافر، إذ الخفيف يعلو صعدا والثقيل ينحدر سفلا، فيمر الدهر. إذ كانا كذلك يتخلصان من وجه التناهي كما امتزجا. قال الشيخ رحمه الله : ومن تأمل القول وجده كله متناقضا، من غير أن يحتاج إلى تكلف الدلالة على إبطال القول سوى تفسيره. أول شيء به أنه أزال النهاية من الوجوه وأثبتها من وجه، فجعل المتناهي غير المتناهي؛ إذ النهاية حد، والحد قصر عما هو أعظم منه، وذلك تدبير غيره فيه، وهو دليل حدث جانب منه؛ وذلك جزء، وبعيد كون كلية الأجزاء المتناهية غير متناهية، لأن ذلك المعنى يتمكن في كل جزء منها ويتصل على أن كل واحد منهما في الوجوه التي لا تتناهى إما أن يكون الآخر فيها فيبطل قوله «امتزجا من جانب»، بل كانا ممتزجين إلا من جانب ثم امتزجا فيه أيضاً،
A question on the description of the sayings of the Dualists. The sayings of the Manichaeans and explanation of their corruption. The Shaykh, may Allah have mercy on him, said: The Manichaeans claimed that things are as they are from the mixture of light and darkness. They were separate: light in the high is infinite in four directions: north, south, east, and west; and darkness in the low likewise, but it has finitude from the direction of contact. Then darkness attacked light and they mixed, and the world came into being from their mixture according to the degree of mixture. Each of them has five genera: redness, whiteness, yellowness, blackness, and greenness. So everything that comes from this genus from the substance of light is good, and what is from the substance of darkness is evil. Likewise, each of them has five senses: hearing, sight, taste, smell, and touch. So what perceives the substance of light by them is good, and what perceives the substance of darkness is evil. Light has a spirit, and darkness has a spirit, and a spirit called Hamama, which is a serpent. It overcame the world to imprison light in it. Light is not sentient, and what is from it is by nature and is entirely good; the Hamama is sentient. Each of them will return to its own place. Then the highest things were found to be the purest, and the lowest the murkiest. Their nature is lightness and heaviness. Their affair is based on repulsion, since the light rises upward and the heavy descends downward, and time passes. Since they are like that, they become separated from the direction of finitude just as they mixed. The Shaykh, may Allah have mercy on him, said: Whoever contemplates this saying finds it entirely contradictory, without needing to exert effort in proving the invalidity of the saying beyond its explanation. The first thing in it is that he removed finitude from some aspects and affirmed it from one aspect, making the finite infinite. For finitude is a limit, and the limit is a restriction from what is greater than it, and that is an arrangement (tadbir) of another in it, and it is evidence of the temporality (hadath) of one side. That is a part, and it is far-fetched that the totality of finite parts is infinite, because that meaning is established in every part of them and connects to the fact that each of them in the directions that are not finite: either the other is in them, which would invalidate his saying 'they mixed from one side', rather they would be mixed except from one side, then they mixed in it also,
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage presents the Manichaean (al-Manawiyya) dualistic cosmology and then refutes it, serving as an example of sectarian refutation in kalam. Maturidi first describes their view: two eternal principles, light and darkness, initially separate. Light is infinite in four horizontal directions; darkness is infinite below but finite at the point of contact. Darkness attacks light, causing their mixture, which results in the material world. Each principle has five colors (genera) and five senses. Whatever comes from light's substance is good; from darkness, evil. Light has a spirit, darkness has a spirit, and a third spirit called Hamama (a serpent) overcomes the world to imprison light. Light is not sentient; the Hamama is sentient. Eventually each principle returns to its own realm; the purest things are highest, the turbid lowest. Due to their natural lightness and heaviness, they gradually separate over time. Then Maturidi states that this entire doctrine is self-contradictory and needs no external refutation. He identifies the first contradiction: they make the principles infinite in some respects but finite in others, thereby making the finite infinite. Finitude implies a limit, which indicates dependence on something greater and points to temporality (hadath). Since each part of the infinite is finite, the whole cannot be infinite. This leads to the problem that if the principles were infinite from all sides, they would be entirely intermingled, contradicting the claim that they mixed only from one side. The passage cuts off while explaining that they would have been mixed except from one side and then mixed in it also.

Key Terms
الثنوية
المنانية
النور
الظلمة
الامتزاج
التناهي
الحد
الخير
الشر
الحواس
الهامة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Manichaean dualistic cosmology is a logically coherent explanation of good and evil.
Correction: Maturidi shows that it is self-contradictory because it claims the principles are both infinite and finite, and this inconsistency alone invalidates the entire theory.

Checkpoint
What is the first contradiction Maturidi identifies in the Manichaean doctrine?
A) They claim both principles are eternal but then say one attacked the other.
B) They make the principles infinite in some respects and finite in others, making the finite infinite and implying temporality.
C) They assign five senses to each principle but only mention four colors.
D) They say light is good and darkness is evil, but then claim both will return to their places.

Key Takeaway
The Manichaean doctrine collapses due to its internal contradiction: it posits the eternal principles as both infinite and finite, which is logically impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at your own life, where do you blame external forces for the evil you see rather than examining your own choices or the oneness of divine decree? This lesson teaches that falsehood contains its own refutation. Will you honestly examine the contradictions in your own worldview today?
?
The Manichaeans believed in two eternal forces. Is there any area of your life where you act as if there is a power independent of Allah—like luck, fate, or your own desires? How does this lesson challenge you to submit entirely to Allah's sole authority?
?
Maturidi did not need external arguments; the false doctrine refuted itself. What false belief might you be holding that, if honestly examined, would collapse under its own weight? Will you set aside your pride and examine it now?

Manichaean Dualist Cosmology Presented
Maturidi reports the Manichaean doctrine of two eternal principles and their mixture.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the core claims of Manichaean dualist cosmology as reported by Imam Maturidi, including the two eternal principles, their mixture, and the roles of the five species, senses, and the Hamama spirit.

Core Idea
Manichaean dualism reduces all existence to a mixture of light and darkness, each with its own substances and spirits.

Imam Maturidi begins his refutation of the Manichaeans by first presenting their worldview in detail. This is essential because one must understand the opponent's position accurately before criticizing it. In this passage, the Manichaeans explain how the world came to be from the interaction of two eternal principles: light (good) and darkness (evil). Let's explore their elaborate cosmology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the detailed categories and the structure of the doctrine.
2
Identify the two principles and their attributes
The passage presents two eternal principles: light and darkness. Note their locations, directions, and finitude. Also note the attack and mixture.
Light is infinite in four directions; darkness is finite at the meeting zone.
3
Examine the five species and five senses
Each principle has five species (colors) and five senses. Understand how these relate to good and evil.
Good comes from light's substance, evil from darkness's.
4
Understand the spirits and the Hamama
Light and darkness each have a spirit; a third spirit called Hamama imprisons light in the world. Note the passive nature of light vs. the active Hamama.
Hamama is sensitive, light is not.
5
Follow the eventual separation
The passage describes how each principle returns to its domain through natural repulsion (light rises, darkness sinks). This sets up refutation.
This shows the internal logic of the system.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة في صفة أقاويل الثنوية أقاويل المنانية وبيان فسادها قال الشيخ رحمه الله : زعمت المنانية أن الأشياء كائنة على ما عليه من امتزاج النور والظلمة. وكانا متباينين: النور في العلو لا يتناهي في أربع جهات شمال وجنوب وصبا ودبور، والظلمة في السفل كذلك، ولها من جهة الالتقاء تناه فبغت الظلمة على النور فامتزجا، فكان العالم من امتزاجهما على قدر الامتزاج ولكل واحد منهما خمسة أجناس : حمرة وبياض وصفرة وسواد وخضرة. فكل شيء مما جاء من هذا الجنس من جوهر النور فهو خير، وما كان من جوهر الظلمة فهو شر . وكذلك لكل واحد منهما حواس خمس: سمع وبصر وذائق وحاسة الشم واللمس فما أدرك جوهر النور بها فهو خير، وما أدرك جوهر الظلمة فهو شر. وللنور روح وللظلمة روح وروح يسمى همامة، وهي حية، فغلب العالم ليحبس النور فيها . والنور ليس بحساس، وما كان منه يكون بالطبع ويكون خيرا كله؛ والهامة حساسة. وسيصير كل واحد منهما إلى حيزه . ثم وجد أعلى الأشياء أصفاها، وأسفلها أكدرها؛ ومن طبعهما الخفة والثقل . وأمرهما على التنافر، إذ الخفيف يعلو صعداً والثقيل ينحدر سفلاً، فيمر الدهر. إذ كانا كذلك يتخلصان من وجه التناهي كما امتزجا.
A question concerning the description of the sayings of the dualists, the sayings of the Manichaeans and the exposition of their corruption. The Shaykh, may God have mercy on him, said: The Manichaeans claimed that things exist as they are from the mixture of light and darkness. They were two distinct things: light in the high [region], infinite in four directions – north, south, east, and west – and darkness in the low [region] likewise, but it has a limit from the direction of meeting. Then darkness attacked light and they mixed, and the world came into being from their mixture according to the degree of mixture. Each of them has five species: red, white, yellow, black, and green. Everything that comes from this kind from the substance of light is good, and whatever is from the substance of darkness is evil. Likewise, each of them has five senses: hearing, sight, taste, smell, and touch. What the substance of light perceives through them is good, and what the substance of darkness perceives is evil. Light has a spirit and darkness has a spirit, and a spirit called Hamama, which is a living [being]; it overcame the world to imprison light in it. Light is not sensitive, and whatever is from it occurs by nature and is entirely good; the Hamama is sensitive. Each of them will return to its own domain. Then the highest things were found to be the purest, and the lowest to be the murkiest; their nature is lightness and heaviness. Their affair is mutual repulsion, for the light rises upward and the heavy sinks downward, and time passes. Since they are so, they become free from the aspect of finitude just as they mixed.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage presents the Manichaean dualist cosmology as reported by Imam Maturidi before refuting it. It is a doctrinal report. The Manichaeans assert two eternal principles: light (good) and darkness (evil). Light is infinite in four directions, darkness is infinite in three directions but finite at the meeting zone. Darkness violently attacks light, and their mixture produces the physical world. Each principle has five elements (colours) and five senses; good originates from light, evil from darkness. They also posit a third entity: a spirit called Hamama (a living being) that imprisons light in the material world. Light is passive and acts by nature (all good), while Hamama is active and sensitive. Eventually, each principle will separate again, and the process of purification occurs through natural repulsion (light rising, darkness sinking). Maturidi sets up this elaborate cosmology to expose its internal contradictions in the subsequent refutation.

Misconception: Manichaean dualism is just a simple myth of good vs. evil.
Correction: The passage shows it includes detailed categories: two principles with specific locations, five species, five senses, and a third spirit Hamama, forming a complex philosophical system.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The Manichaeans explain the world's existence as a temporary mixture of two eternal principles, light and darkness, each with its own categories and eventual separation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt that evil is as powerful as good, as if they are two equal forces battling in the world? What does this false belief say about your trust in Allah's sole sovereignty and the reality that He alone creates both good and evil?
?
The Manichaeans believed that good things come from light and evil from darkness. In your daily life, do you sometimes attribute good to your own efforts and evil to external circumstances? How does this lesson expose that as a hidden form of dualism that diminishes your reliance on Allah?
?
The Hamama spirit imprisoned light in the world, leading to despair of liberation. Do you ever feel that your soul is trapped by worldly desires or that you cannot escape your sins? What is the Islamic alternative to this despairing worldview, and how can you remind yourself of it when you feel trapped?

The Self-Contradiction of Dualism
Maturidi's first argument against dualism: the contradiction of finite and infinite.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi exposes the internal contradiction in the Manichaean claim that light is infinite in some directions and finite in others, leading to absurdity.

Core Idea
Dualism collapses when its own claims about infinity become self-contradictory.

Maturidi begins his refutation by stating that the Manichaean doctrine is self-contradictory and needs no external proof – simply explaining it suffices. He then identifies the first contradiction: the Manichaeans assert that light is infinite in all directions but darkness is finite, yet they claim mixture occurs from one side. This leads to a logical absurdity. Let us follow his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how Maturidi frames the argument as a self-contradiction.
2
Identify the contradictory claims
Maturidi points out that the Manichaeans affirm finitude from one aspect and negate it from others. Find where that happens.
3
Understand why it leads to absurdity
If light is infinite in all directions, darkness cannot approach it from a side without already being inside it. This invalidates the concept of mixture from one side.
This is the key logical move.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشيخ رحمه الله : ومن تأمل القول وجده كله متناقضا، من غير أن يحتاج إلى تكلف الدلالة على إبطال القول سوى تفسيره. أول شيء به أنه أزال النهاية من الوجوه وأثبتها من وجه، فجعل المتناهي غير المتناهي؛ إذ النهاية حد، والحد قصر عما هو أعظم منه، وذلك تدبير غيره فيه، وهو دليل حدث جانب منه ؛ وذلك جزء، وبعيد كون كلية الأجزاء المتناهية غير متناهية ، لأن ذلك المعنى يتمكن في كل جزء منها ويتصل على أن كل واحد منهما في الوجوه التي لا تتناهي إما أن يكون الآخر فيها فيبطل قوله «امتزجا من جانب»، بل كانا ممتزجين إلا من جانب ثم امتزجا فيه أيضا، وإن لم يكن زال كل واحد منهما عن الأوجه الأربعة التي هي للآخر، فصار من متناهيا . والله الموفق. تلك الوجوه ثم إن كان من طبع السفلى التسفل والعلوي العلو - وذلك معنى التنافر وإليه مرجع العاقبة - فكيف صار السفلى يذهب صعدا، وذلك طبع العالي الصافي، وهو معنى الخير؛ فقد صار من السفلى الأمران جميعا، فبطل المعنى الذي له لزم القول باثنين. ثم من طبع العلوي النفار إلى العلو ، ولم يقم بوفاء ذلك ولا امتنع به عما كان بجوهر ينحدر حتى ارتفع عليه، وخلق العالم بحبسه ؛ فكيف يطمعون أن يتخلص من يدي الهامة ؟ وهي مع ذلك حساسة فعالة بالحيل أوثقته وقيدته وحبسته وليست له قوة يتخلص بها، وبطبعه لم يمتنع عند التخلية ؛ فكيف يتخلص بعد الوثاق ؟ إلا أن يقول : تخل الهامة سبيله، فيجعلها فاعلة الخير. وبعد، فإن جوهر الظلمة إن كان هو رأى النور وهو الذي آنس النور ليحبسه فهو الموصوف بالعلم والرؤية لا الذي لم يره ليتحصن منه ولم يعلم ما به يتخلص من قهره. فإذا العلم والرؤية والقدرة والغنى والشرف كله في جوهر الظلمة، والقهر والجهل والعجز والذل والهوان في جوهر النور. فإن كان ذا كله خيرا والأول كله شرا فما أبصركم بالخير والشر. وكذلك عندكم إن النور فعله طباع والهامة فعلها اختيار والعالم أنشأته الهامة، بطل القول باثنين ؛ بل العالم كله فعل الواحد، لكنه مزج أجزاءه بأجزاء الآخر. ولو كان الآخر بما يفعل به وفيه يصير آخر لتحصيل القول بالاثنين لكان كل ذي طبع هو من به وفيه العالم، فيصير القول بما لا يحصى عدده. ثم إذ كانت الظلمة التي بغت على النور ثم يتخلص منها، فأما أن تكون هي
The Shaykh, may God have mercy on him, said: Whoever ponders this saying finds it entirely contradictory, without needing to burden oneself with proof to invalidate the saying other than explaining it. The first thing about it is that it negates finitude from some aspects and affirms it from one aspect, making the finite infinite; for finitude is a limit, and a limit is a restriction from what is greater than it, and that is the management of something else in it, and it is evidence of the temporality of a side of it; and that is a part, and it is far-fetched that the totality of finite parts be infinite, because that meaning is possible in every part of them and connects, such that each of them in the aspects that are infinite, either the other is in them, which invalidates his statement 'they mixed from one side' – rather they were mixed except from one side, then they mixed in it also – or if one of them has not departed from the four aspects that belong to the other, then it becomes finite from those aspects. And God is the giver of success. Those aspects: then if it is the nature of the lower to go down and the higher to go up – and that is the meaning of repulsion and to it the final result refers – then how did the lower go upward, while that is the nature of the high pure, and it is the meaning of good? Thus both affairs have come from the lower, so the meaning by which one was compelled to affirm two [principles] is invalidated. Then, from the nature of the higher is aversion to upward [movement]? It did not fulfill that, nor did it abstain by it from what was in a substance descending until it rose over it, and created the world by imprisoning it. So how do they hope that it will escape from the hands of the Hamama? And it, despite that, is sensitive, active with tricks; it bound it, tied it, imprisoned it, and it has no power to escape, and by its nature it did not resist when released; so how can it escape after being bound? Unless one says: the Hamama releases its way, thus making it a doer of good. Moreover, if the substance of darkness saw the light and it is the one that perceived the light to imprison it, then it is described with knowledge and sight, not the one that did not see it to protect itself from it and did not know by what to escape its domination. Then knowledge, sight, power, wealth, and honor are all in the substance of darkness, while domination, ignorance, impotence, lowliness, and humiliation are in the substance of light. If all that is good and the first is all evil, then how discerning are you of good and evil! Likewise, according to you, the action of light is by nature and the action of the Hamama is by choice, and the world was created by the Hamama, then the statement of two [principles] is invalidated; rather, the entire world is the act of the One, but He mixed its parts with parts of the other. And if the other, by what it does in and to it, becomes another to achieve the statement of two [principles], then every possessor of a nature is the one through whom and in whom the world exists, and the statement would become of uncountable number. Then, since darkness attacked light and then escapes from it, either it is ...
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage is a multipronged refutation of Manichaean dualism. Maturidi begins by stating that the doctrine is self-contradictory: mere explanation suffices. The first argument concerns finitude and infinity: the Manichaeans affirm light infinite in four directions but darkness finite at the meeting point, yet claim mixture occurs from one side – this leads to absurdity because if light is infinite in all directions, darkness cannot attack it from a side without already being mixed. The second argument uses their own principle of repulsion: if darkness naturally sinks and light rises, how did darkness go upward to attack light? That would mean darkness acts against its nature, collapsing the distinction. The third argument focuses on the Hamama (the imprisoning spirit): if light is passive and weak, it cannot resist; if the Hamama releases it, then the Hamama does good, contradicting its evil nature. The fourth argument inverts values: darkness is described as knowing, seeing, and powerful (to plan and capture light), while light is ignorant and powerless – but the Manichaeans call light 'good' and darkness 'evil', which is inconsistent. The fifth argument: if only the Hamama acts by choice and creates the world, then the world is the act of one agent, not two – the true Creator is one. Finally, Maturidi reduces dualism to absurdity: if every nature that produces effects is a divine principle, there would be countless gods. The passage concludes mid-sentence with a final dilemma about darkness escaping.

Key Terms
متناقض
النهاية
الحد
المتناهي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That dualism (light and darkness as eternal principles) is a logically consistent worldview.
Correction: Maturidi shows that the dualist claims about finitude and infinity are inherently contradictory, making dualism irrational.

Checkpoint
What is the main logical problem Maturidi identifies in the Manichaean claim about light and darkness?
A) Light is infinite but darkness attacks it from one side
B) Darkness is naturally evil and cannot do good
C) The universe is too complex for two creators
D) The Hamama cannot imprison light

Key Takeaway
Maturidi's first argument refutes dualism by showing that its own claims about infinity and finitude are logically inconsistent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Maturidi says the dualist's claim is contradictory 'without needing to burden oneself with proof, other than explaining it.' Think about a belief you hold that you have never examined closely. What would happen if you simply articulated it aloud? Would it collapse under its own weight? Commit today to honestly examine one such belief.
?
If a finite darkness can approach an infinite light 'from one side,' does that not make the light finite on that side? In your own life, where do you try to hold onto two incompatible ideas—like claiming absolute trust in God while refusing to let go of your own plans? What would it cost you to resolve that contradiction?
?
Maturidi uses pure logic to expose an absurdity in dualism. When was the last time you allowed your intellect to challenge a comfortable but inconsistent belief you have? What is stopping you from doing that today?

The Contradiction of Natures in Dualism
Maturidi refutes dualism by exposing contradictions in the natures of light and darkness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the Manichaeans' own principle of natural repulsion to show that darkness cannot attack light.

Core Idea
If darkness naturally sinks, how can it rise to attack light? Dualism contradicts its own principles.

Maturidi now turns to the Manichaean claim that darkness and light have opposite natures: darkness tends downward, light upward, and they repel each other. He asks a devastating question: if darkness naturally sinks, how did it manage to rise upward to attack light? This undermines the entire dualist narrative.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the assumption about natural repulsion.
2
Identify the logical problem
Maturidi points out that if darkness naturally goes down, it cannot go up to attack light. Therefore, either darkness changed its nature or the attack never happened.
3
Consider the Hamama argument
Then Maturidi argues that even if the Hamama imprisoned light, it cannot escape because it is weak, and if the Hamama releases it, then the Hamama does good, contradicting its evil nature.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever accepted a story about good and evil without testing its logical consistency? What in your life today might be built on a similar inconsistency, and are you willing to dismantle it?
?
If darkness cannot rise by its own nature, how does the refutation of dualism remind you that evil has no independent power? How should this change the way you fear hardship or temptation?
?
Maturidi exposes that the spirit imprisoning light, if it releases it, does good. Is there an area where you have judged someone or something as purely evil, only to find that it could be a means of good? Are you ready to see good in unexpected places?

The Inversion of Attributes and Unity of Action
Maturidi refutes dualism by inverting its value system and arguing for one creator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi argues that the Manichaean attribution of knowledge and power to darkness and ignorance to light inverts their value system, and that the world must be the act of one creator.

Core Idea
If darkness is knowing and powerful, it cannot be evil; and if darkness creates the world, there is only one creator.

Maturidi continues his refutation by examining the attributes the Manichaeans assign to light and darkness. He finds that darkness is described as knowledgeable, seeing, and powerful (to capture light), while light is ignorant and weak. This contradicts the Manichaean claim that light is good and darkness evil. Furthermore, if the Hamama (darkness) creates the world by choice, then the world is the act of one – not two – and the dualist claim collapses.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Pay attention to the attributes assigned to each principle.
2
Analyze the inversion
Maturidi points out that darkness has knowledge, sight, and power, while light has ignorance and weakness. If these are the attributes, then darkness has the qualities of good and light has those of evil – the opposite of what dualists claim.
3
Understand the unity argument
If the Hamama creates the world by choice, then the world is the act of one agent. If every nature that acts counts as a principle, there would be countless gods, leading to absurdity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشيخ رحمه الله : ومن تأمل القول وجده كله متناقضا، من غير أن يحتاج إلى تكلف الدلالة على إبطال القول سوى تفسيره. أول شيء به أنه أزال النهاية من الوجوه وأثبتها من وجه، فجعل المتناهي غير المتناهي؛ إذ النهاية حد، والحد قصر عما هو أعظم منه، وذلك تدبير غيره فيه، وهو دليل حدث جانب منه ؛ وذلك جزء، وبعيد كون كلية الأجزاء المتناهية غير متناهية ، لأن ذلك المعنى يتمكن في كل جزء منها ويتصل على أن كل واحد منهما في الوجوه التي لا تتناهي إما أن يكون الآخر فيها فيبطل قوله «امتزجا من جانب»، بل كانا ممتزجين إلا من جانب ثم امتزجا فيه أيضا، وإن لم يكن زال كل واحد منهما عن الأوجه الأربعة التي هي للآخر، فصار من متناهيا . والله الموفق. تلك الوجوه ثم إن كان من طبع السفلى التسفل والعلوي العلو - وذلك معنى التنافر وإليه مرجع العاقبة - فكيف صار السفلى يذهب صعدا، وذلك طبع العالي الصافي، وهو معنى الخير؛ فقد صار من السفلى الأمران جميعا، فبطل المعنى الذي له لزم القول باثنين. ثم من طبع العلوي النفار إلى العلو ، ولم يقم بوفاء ذلك ولا امتنع به عما كان بجوهر ينحدر حتى ارتفع عليه، وخلق العالم بحبسه ؛ فكيف يطمعون أن يتخلص من يدي الهامة ؟ وهي مع ذلك حساسة فعالة بالحيل أوثقته وقيدته وحبسته وليست له قوة يتخلص بها، وبطبعه لم يمتنع عند التخلية ؛ فكيف يتخلص بعد الوثاق ؟ إلا أن يقول : تخل الهامة سبيله، فيجعلها فاعلة الخير. وبعد، فإن جوهر الظلمة إن كان هو رأى النور وهو الذي آنس النور ليحبسه فهو الموصوف بالعلم والرؤية لا الذي لم يره ليتحصن منه ولم يعلم ما به يتخلص من قهره. فإذا العلم والرؤية والقدرة والغنى والشرف كله في جوهر الظلمة، والقهر والجهل والعجز والذل والهوان في جوهر النور. فإن كان ذا كله خيرا والأول كله شرا فما أبصركم بالخير والشر. وكذلك عندكم إن النور فعله طباع والهامة فعلها اختيار والعالم أنشأته الهامة، بطل القول باثنين ؛ بل العالم كله فعل الواحد، لكنه مزج أجزاءه بأجزاء الآخر. ولو كان الآخر بما يفعل به وفيه يصير آخر لتحصيل القول بالاثنين لكان كل ذي طبع هو من به وفيه العالم، فيصير القول بما لا يحصى عدده. ثم إذ كانت الظلمة التي بغت على النور ثم يتخلص منها، فأما أن تكون هي
The Shaykh, may God have mercy on him, said: Whoever ponders this saying finds it entirely contradictory, without needing to burden oneself with proof to invalidate the saying other than explaining it. The first thing about it is that it negates finitude from some aspects and affirms it from one aspect, making the finite infinite; for finitude is a limit, and a limit is a restriction from what is greater than it, and that is the management of something else in it, and it is evidence of the temporality of a side of it; and that is a part, and it is far-fetched that the totality of finite parts be infinite, because that meaning is possible in every part of them and connects, such that each of them in the aspects that are infinite, either the other is in them, which invalidates his statement 'they mixed from one side' – rather they were mixed except from one side, then they mixed in it also – or if one of them has not departed from the four aspects that belong to the other, then it becomes finite from those aspects. And God is the giver of success. Those aspects: then if it is the nature of the lower to go down and the higher to go up – and that is the meaning of repulsion and to it the final result refers – then how did the lower go upward, while that is the nature of the high pure, and it is the meaning of good? Thus both affairs have come from the lower, so the meaning by which one was compelled to affirm two [principles] is invalidated. Then, from the nature of the higher is aversion to upward [movement]? It did not fulfill that, nor did it abstain by it from what was in a substance descending until it rose over it, and created the world by imprisoning it. So how do they hope that it will escape from the hands of the Hamama? And it, despite that, is sensitive, active with tricks; it bound it, tied it, imprisoned it, and it has no power to escape, and by its nature it did not resist when released; so how can it escape after being bound? Unless one says: the Hamama releases its way, thus making it a doer of good. Moreover, if the substance of darkness saw the light and it is the one that perceived the light to imprison it, then it is described with knowledge and sight, not the one that did not see it to protect itself from it and did not know by what to escape its domination. Then knowledge, sight, power, wealth, and honor are all in the substance of darkness, while domination, ignorance, impotence, lowliness, and humiliation are in the substance of light. If all that is good and the first is all evil, then how discerning are you of good and evil! Likewise, according to you, the action of light is by nature and the action of the Hamama is by choice, and the world was created by the Hamama, then the statement of two [principles] is invalidated; rather, the entire world is the act of the One, but He mixed its parts with parts of the other. And if the other, by what it does in and to it, becomes another to achieve the statement of two [principles], then every possessor of a nature is the one through whom and in whom the world exists, and the statement would become of uncountable number. Then, since darkness attacked light and then escapes from it, either it is ...
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage is a multipronged refutation of Manichaean dualism. Maturidi begins by stating that the doctrine is self-contradictory: mere explanation suffices. The first argument concerns finitude and infinity: the Manichaeans affirm light infinite in four directions but darkness finite at the meeting point, yet claim mixture occurs from one side – this leads to absurdity because if light is infinite in all directions, darkness cannot attack it from a side without already being mixed. The second argument uses their own principle of repulsion: if darkness naturally sinks and light rises, how did darkness go upward to attack light? That would mean darkness acts against its nature, collapsing the distinction. The third argument focuses on the Hamama (the imprisoning spirit): if light is passive and weak, it cannot resist; if the Hamama releases it, then the Hamama does good, contradicting its evil nature. The fourth argument inverts values: darkness is described as knowing, seeing, and powerful (to plan and capture light), while light is ignorant and powerless – but the Manichaeans call light 'good' and darkness 'evil', which is inconsistent. The fifth argument: if only the Hamama acts by choice and creates the world, then the world is the act of one agent, not two – the true Creator is one. Finally, Maturidi reduces dualism to absurdity: if every nature that produces effects is a divine principle, there would be countless gods. The passage concludes mid-sentence with a final dilemma about darkness escaping.

طباع
اختيار
الواحد

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That dualism consistently attributes good to light and evil to darkness.
Correction: Maturidi shows that the attributes given to darkness (knowledge, power) imply it is good, while light's attributes (ignorance, weakness) imply it is evil, inverting the dualist value system.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi identify as a key inconsistency in the Manichaean description of light and darkness?
A) Darkness is described as knowing and powerful, yet claimed to be evil
B) Light is infinite in all directions
C) The Hamama is not a real entity
D) The world was created by both

Key Takeaway
Maturidi's refutation shows that dualism's own descriptions of light and darkness undermine its value system and point to one creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see darkness and struggle in your own life, do you instinctively attribute them to an external evil force or to your own shortcomings? How does Maturidi's inversion challenge you to reconsider who actually possesses knowledge and power in those situations? Will you this week examine one trial and identify what attributes you are assigning to whom?
?
Do you sometimes compartmentalize your good deeds as from Allah and your sins as from yourself or shaytan? How does the unity of action—that one creator produced the entire world including both elements—call you to take full responsibility for your choices before Allah? What would change if you owned every action as your own?
?
Think of a person or group you have labeled as entirely 'bad' or 'good'. Using Maturidi's method, what attributes do they actually exhibit that contradict your label? Will you commit to re-evaluating one such judgment this week with logical scrutiny, starting with the source of those attributes?

Maturidi's Reductio Against Dualism
Maturidi uses reductio ad absurdum to invert dualist moral categories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Maturidi uses a reductio ad absurdum argument to expose the inconsistency of the dualist claim that light is good and darkness is evil.

Core Idea
Maturidi flips the dualists' premise: if darkness imprisons light, then darkness has all the good attributes.

In this passage, Imam Maturidi addresses the Manichaean dualists who claim that light is good and darkness is evil. He takes their own narrative—that darkness attacks and imprisons light—and shows that it logically leads to the opposite conclusion: darkness would actually possess knowledge, power, and honor, while light would be ignorant and weak. This clever argument forces the dualists to reconsider their categorizations of good and evil.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text and its translation to grasp the argument's flow. Notice the conditional structure starting with 'إذا'.
2
Identify the dualist premise
Maturidi begins by stating the dualist claim: darkness sees light and imprisons it. Note that this is the premise he will turn against them.
The dualists believe darkness is the source of evil, yet they attribute action to it.
3
Follow the logical consequence
If darkness performed the act of seeing and imprisoning, then it must have knowledge, sight, and power. Light, being passive, lacks these. See how Maturidi reverses the moral categories.
He lists knowledge, sight, power, wealth, honor on darkness's side, and domination, ignorance, inability, lowliness, contempt on light's side.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Maturidi ends with a sarcastic rhetorical question: 'How clear-sighted are you regarding good and evil?' This forces the dualist to admit the absurdity of their position.
The argument does not require new premises; it uses only what the dualists already accept.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن جوهر الظلمة إن كان هو رأى النور وهو الذي آنس النور ليحبسه فهو الموصوف بالعلم والرؤية لا الذي لم يره ليتحصن منه ولم يعلم ما به يتخلص من قهره. فإذا العلم والرؤية والقدرة والغنى والشرف كله في جوهر الظلمة، والقهر والجهل والعجز والذل والهوان في جوهر النور. فإن كان ذا كله خيرا والأول كله شراً فما أبصركم بالخير والشر.
For if the essence of darkness is the one that saw the light and is the one that perceived the light to imprison it, then it is described with knowledge and sight, not the one that did not see it to protect itself from it nor knew by what to escape from its domination. So then knowledge, sight, power, wealth, honor — all of them are in the essence of darkness, while domination, ignorance, inability, lowliness, and contempt are in the essence of light. If this whole (second set) is good and the first whole is evil, then how clear-sighted are you regarding good and evil?
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This is a reductio ad absurdum argument against the dualist narrative. According to the Manichaean story, darkness (the lower principle) attacks light, sees it, and imprisons it. If so, darkness is the one that possesses sight, knowledge, and power to act. Light, being the passive victim, is ignorant, weak, and dominated. Thus, darkness would actually possess all the attributes associated with good (knowledge, power, honor), while light would have the attributes of evil (ignorance, weakness, humiliation). This completely reverses the dualists' own value judgments, where light is good and darkness is evil. The author sarcastically remarks that the dualists have a strange perception of good and evil if they maintain their position. The argument is presented as a direct consequence of the dualists' premises.

Key Terms
جوهر الظلمة
العلم
الرؤية
القدرة
الخير
الشر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think Maturidi is actually claiming that darkness possesses attributes of perfection, endorsing dualism.
Correction: Maturidi is not endorsing that darkness is good. He is merely showing that the dualists' own story logically leads to that conclusion, which they must reject. It is a reductio ad absurdum, not a positive assertion.

Checkpoint
In this argument, what does Maturidi say darkness would possess if it imprisoned light?
A) Ignorance and weakness
B) Knowledge, sight, and power
C) Evil and corruption
D) Light and goodness

Key Takeaway
Maturidi's reductio shows that the dualist narrative of darkness imprisoning light logically leads to the absurd conclusion that darkness possesses all good attributes, thereby undermining its own moral framework.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a conviction you hold about what is 'good' in the world. Have you ever allowed that conviction to go unchallenged? What if, when examined carefully, the very attributes you assign to 'good' actually belong to what you considered 'evil'? Are you prepared to have your moral categories inverted? If not, are you willing to ask yourself why?
?
Maturidi's reductio forces the dualists to confront the logical outcome of their own narrative. Is there a narrative you tell yourself about your own life—about who is right or wrong, about your own purity or darkness—that you have never followed to its logical end? What might that end reveal about your true allegiance?
?
The lesson ends with a sarcastic remark about being 'clear-sighted regarding good and evil'. When is the last time you truly questioned your own clarity on moral matters? Are you more interested in being right or in being honest about the possibility that you might be the one in ignorance?

The Logical Impossibility of Light's Separation from Darkness
Maturidi argues against dualist separation of light from darkness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's logical argument against the dualist claim that light can eventually separate from darkness.

Core Idea
If light is mixed with darkness, its freedom leads to an infinite regress—impossible.

The dualists argued that light and darkness are eternal principles that become mixed, but will eventually separate. Maturidi systematically dismantles this claim by showing that any scenario of separation leads to a logical contradiction. This passage demonstrates his method of refuting opponents by accepting their premises and showing their absurd conclusions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the flow of the argument.
Notice the dense, technical style of Maturidi's reasoning.
2
Identify the two possibilities considered
Maturidi examines two ways light might be freed: (1) by its own essence, or (2) by darkness pushing it away. Find where each is discussed.
3
Understand why each possibility fails
For each scenario, Maturidi shows a fatal flaw: infinite space for the first, and self-contradiction for the second. Trace the logic step by step.
The infinite space argument is key: beyond the mixture, there is no limit.
4
Reflect on the overall conclusion
Maturidi concludes that separation is meaningless ('la ma'na liltakhallus'). Consider how this refutes the dualist position without invoking scripture.
This is a purely rational argument based on shared premises.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إذ كانت الظلمة التي بغت على النور ثم يتخلص منها، فأما أن يكون التخلص منها بالجوهر فذلك محال، لأنه لم يمتنع منها به مع ما يجب تخلص أجزائه من حبس الهمامة، وليس فيها علاه موضع يسير إليه ما انتزع منها؛ إذ غير هذا الجانب غير متناه، وهو بالتخلص يرجع إلى ما لا نهاية، فلا يجد لنفسه موضع قرار. فلا معنى للتخلص إلا أن تكون الظلمة تدفعه عن نفسها، فيكون دفعه خيرا، إذ كان حبسه شراً. مع ما إذا دفعت أجزاءه، وما علا ليس إلا أجزاؤه، فهو يدخل بعضه بعضاً، وذلك نهاية. لكنه كانت تحبسه في جوهره ثم قهرت كلية النور فجعلته سجنا لنفسها تحبس فيه عدوها، فيصير عدوها بجوهره حبيسا لنفسه. وبعد، فإن الظلمة ليس لها في غير وجه الامتزاج حد، فهو إلى ما ذا يصير بالتخلص؟ فهو يبيّن أن لا معنى للتخلص.
Then, since it is the darkness that attacked the light and then it is freed from it, is the freedom from it by essence? That is impossible, because it did not resist it by essence with what necessitates the freedom of its parts from the imprisonment of the owl, and there is not in it above a place to which what is extracted from it might go; for other than this side is infinite, and it, by being freed, returns to what has no end, so it finds for itself no place of stability. So there is no meaning to freedom unless the darkness pushes it away from itself, in which case its pushing would be good, since its imprisonment was evil. Along with that, when it (darkness) pushes its parts, and what is above is nothing but its parts, then it enters some of it into some other, and that is an end. But it (darkness) was imprisoning it in its essence, then it overcame the whole of light and made it a prison for itself, imprisoning in it its enemy, so its enemy becomes by its essence imprisoned in itself. And moreover, darkness has no limit other than the face of mixture, so to what would it become by freedom? That shows that there is no meaning to freedom.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed argument against the dualist concept of the eventual separation of light from darkness. The author considers the possibility of light being freed from darkness. If freedom is by essence, that is impossible because light did not resist imprisonment by its own essence; its parts are mixed and held by the owl (darkness). Moreover, beyond the mixture there is infinite space (the other side is infinite), so light would have nowhere to settle. Even if darkness itself pushes light away, that would imply darkness is good for releasing light, but then darkness is the agent of good. The author also points out a paradox: if darkness pushes light's parts, the parts below it are also its own parts, leading to self-containment. Furthermore, darkness has no boundary except the mixture, so what would light become when freed? The argument concludes that the idea of escape from darkness is incoherent. The structure follows the dualist story and demonstrates its logical impossibility at each step.

Key Terms
التخلص
الامتزاج
غير متناه
الهمامة
الظلمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think this is a scientific argument about physical intermingling of light and darkness.
Correction: It is actually a logical argument based on the dualists' own premises about infinite space and the nature of light and darkness as eternal substances.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, why is the separation of light from darkness impossible?
A) Light is too weak to move
B) There is no finite place for the separated light to go since the other side is infinite
C) Darkness refuses to let go
D) The mixing is permanent by nature

Key Takeaway
Maturidi shows that the dualist idea of separation is logically impossible because any scenario leads to an infinite regress or self-contradiction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you holding onto a belief in your life that, when examined honestly, leads to logical contradictions? Commit today to investigate one such belief with the same rigor Maturidi applied to dualism.
?
The dualists refused to accept the impossibility of separation, clinging to their idea. Is there an area in your life where you resist God's truth because it would require you to give up a cherished notion? What would it look like to surrender that notion today?
?
Maturidi shows that wrong premises lead to endless regress and confusion. In your own spiritual life, are you building on premises that do not align with sound aqeedah? Identify one premise and ask Him to correct it.

Good Cannot Come from Imprisoned Light: Maturidi's Critique of Dualism
Maturidi questions how good can come from light if it is powerless and imprisoned.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that the dualist claim of light as the source of all good is self-contradictory because light is described as imprisoned and powerless.

Core Idea
Imprisoned power cannot produce good — the dualist narrative defeats itself.

Maturidi continues his critique of dualism by focusing on a logical inconsistency. The dualists claim that all good originates from light, but their own story describes light as dominated and imprisoned by darkness. In this passage, Maturidi asks a pointed question: how can a powerless, imprisoned being be the source of good? The argument is sharp and rhetorical, exposing the contradiction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm and rhetorical questioning come through.
Notice that Maturidi uses a series of rhetorical questions to drive his point.
2
Identify the dualist claim
The passage begins by stating the dualist position: all good in the world is from the essence of light. This is what Maturidi is about to critique.
3
Spot the contradiction
Maturidi immediately points out that light is described as 'dominated' (المقهور) and 'imprisoned' (المحبوس). How can something powerless produce good? This is the core of his objection.
The dualist narrative itself says light is passive, so it cannot be an active source of good.
4
Follow the logic of action and imprisonment
Maturidi explains that all action comes from darkness, which imprisons light. Light merely remains in prison. Any supposed positive action from light (casting parts into imprisonment) is actually evil. Thus, light cannot be the source of good.
This step unpacks the detailed reasoning in the middle of the passage.
5
Reflect on the final rhetorical question
The passage ends with a poignant question: 'How can it be the kingdom of good, while it is entirely in deliverance, and it is not prevented?' This underscores the absurdity of the dualist claim.
The question is meant to be unanswerable, solidifying Maturidi's critique.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشيخ رحمه الله: ثم العجب من قولهم إن الخير كله في العالم من جوهر النور؛ فمن أين يكون منه الخير وهو المقهور المحبوس؟ والفعل كله من الآخر ليحبسه به، فليس من النور غير البقاء في سجن الآخر ووثاقه، فمن أين يجيئ منه خير؟ إلا أن يرى ذلك سائر الأجزاء التي لم تبغ عليه، فيلقى أجزاءه في حبس أجزاء آخر، وذلك هو الشر؛ وأنى لملك الخير، وهو كله في الخلاص، وهو غير ممنوع.
The Shaykh, may God have mercy on him, said: Then the wonder is from their statement that all good in the world is from the essence of light; so from where does good come from it when it is the dominated, the imprisoned? And all action is from the other to imprison it by it, so from light there is nothing except remaining in the prison of the other and its shackles, so from where does good come from it? Unless he sees that other parts that did not attack it, so it casts its parts into the imprisonment of the parts of the other, and that is evil; and how is it the kingdom of good, while it is entirely in deliverance, and it is not prevented?
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This is an objection from the author himself (introduced by 'said the Shaykh') against the dualist claim that all good in the world originates from light. The author points out the contradiction: light is described as dominated, imprisoned, and powerless. It is not acting but being acted upon. The only action is from darkness, which imprisons light. Therefore, light cannot be the source of good. If anything, light's parts are cast into imprisonment, which is evil. The author asks rhetorically how light can be the kingdom of good when it is entirely concerned with deliverance and is not even able to achieve it. The argument follows directly from the dualist narrative: if light is passive and suffering, it cannot produce good.

Key Terms

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Maturidi denies that light has any positive role in the world.
Correction: Maturidi is not making an independent claim about light; he is only criticizing the dualist inconsistency. He argues that the dualist narrative itself makes light powerless, so it cannot be the source of good.

Checkpoint
What is Maturidi's main objection in this passage?
A) Light is actually evil
B) Light cannot be the source of good because it is imprisoned and dominated
C) Darkness is the source of good
D) The world is not created

Key Takeaway
Maturidi exposes the internal contradiction in dualism: if light is imprisoned and powerless, it cannot be the source of good.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you relying on any 'source of good' in your life that is actually powerless or imprisoned? What would it mean to redirect your trust to the only One who is truly sovereign and free?
?
Maturidi shows that a claim can fall apart when examined internally. Is there a belief you hold that, when you really think about it, contradicts itself? What would it cost you to let go of that inconsistency?
?
The dualists thought light was the source of good, but it could not even free itself. What 'good' have you been chasing that leaves you more imprisoned? How does this passage call you to examine the true source of your deliverance?

The Contradiction of Essential Difference and Mixture
Maturidi exposes the contradiction between essential difference and the possibility of mixture.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical contradiction in the dualist claim that two essentially different principles can mix.

Core Idea
If two things are essentially different, they cannot mix — the dualists want both.

Imam Maturidi sharpens his critique of dualist cosmology with a precise logical argument. The dualists hold that light and darkness are fundamentally distinct in essence (mutabayan). Yet they also claim that the world arises from their mixture. Maturidi points out that these two claims cannot both be true. In this passage, he exposes the contradiction with surgical clarity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and English translation. Note the key terms: tabayun (essential difference), jawhar (essence), imtizaj (mixture).
2
Identify the two claims
The dualists claim both essential difference (by essence) and mixture. Underline these two in the text.
3
Understand the contradiction
If two things are essentially different, they cannot mix, because mixture requires some common ground or interaction. Ask: why does essential difference rule out mixture?
This is the core logical insight.
4
Consider the dualists' response
Maturidi notes that dualists do not see mixture as something else (i.e., they do not posit a third thing). This closes their escape route. How does this strengthen the contradiction?
5
Reflect on the rhetorical question
The passage ends with a question: 'Was there not mixture?' This forces the opponent to admit mixture exists, but their own principle denies its possibility. How does this final question seal the argument?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم التناقض أنهم جعلوا التباين بالجوهر فمحال امتزاجهما وهما بالجوهر متباينان. وذلك قائم بحاله؛ إذ هم لا يرون الامتزاج غيرًا. على أنه يقال لهم: الامتزاج أليس كان؟
Then the contradiction is that they made essential difference (tabayun) by essence, so their mixture is impossible while they are essentially different. And that is established in its state; for they do not see mixture as otherwise. Moreover, it is said to them: Was not the mixture?
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This short passage highlights a fundamental logical contradiction in the dualist position. The dualists claim that light and darkness are essentially different (mutabayan) from each other. But if they are essentially different, they cannot mix, because mixing requires some commonality or mutual interaction. However, the dualists also assert that the world is a mixture of the two. This is a direct contradiction. The author notes that the dualists themselves do not view mixture as something else (i.e., they do not offer a third concept). The passage ends with a rhetorical question: 'Was there not mixture?'—meaning the dualists cannot deny the mixture, but their premise of essential difference makes mixture impossible. The argument is concise but devastating: the dualists cannot have both essential difference and mixture.

Key Terms
التباين
الجوهر
الامتزاج
متباينان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Maturidi denies the possibility of mixture in general
Correction: He is specifically refuting the dualist claim that two essentially different principles can mix.

Checkpoint
What contradiction does Maturidi point out in the dualist position?
A) They say light is good but darkness is evil
B) They claim the principles are essentially different yet also claim they mix
C) They say darkness is eternal but light is created
D) They believe the world is created by a single principle

Key Takeaway
Essential difference and mixture are logically incompatible; the dualists cannot have both without contradiction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When have you held two beliefs that cannot both be true because they contradict each other, yet you clung to both? What might you be afraid to let go of if you resolved that contradiction?
?
The dualists refused to give up either essential difference or mixture because both were central to their worldview. Is there an inconsistency in your own worldview that you have been ignoring because abandoning it would be too costly?
?
Maturidi's rhetorical question 'Was there not mixture?' forces the dualist to admit the reality of mixture, which then exposes the contradiction. What question might someone ask you that would expose a hidden inconsistency between your beliefs and your actions?

Impossibility of Extricating Light from Darkness
Maturidi refutes Manichaean claim of light extraction from darkness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's logical proof that the Manichaean concept of light being extracted from darkness is impossible.

Core Idea
Extracting light from infinite darkness is impossible because light would have nowhere to go.

Maturidi here engages with the dualist cosmology of the Manichaeans, who posited two eternal principles of light and darkness. He shows that their claim of light being able to escape from darkness is logically incoherent. The argument proceeds by examining the implications of darkness being infinite and the nature of light as a substance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the English translation to get a feel for Maturidi's reasoning.
The passage is dense; focus on the flow of the argument.
2
Identify key premises
Notice that Maturidi assumes darkness is infinite (غير متناه) and light is a substance. These are key to the refutation.
The Manichaeans agreed that darkness is infinite in extent.
3
Follow the logical steps
Trace the argument: first, if light is extracted, it goes to infinity (no stable place). Second, if darkness pushes light, that would be good (contradiction). Third, parts of light would just intermix. Fourth, darkness has no limit except in mixture.
Each step shows a different absurdity.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Maturidi concludes that extrication is meaningless and ends with a declaration of divine power. Ask yourself what this shows about dualism in general.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التخلص منها بالجوهر فذلك محال، لأنه لم يمتنع منها بما يجب تخلص أجزائه من حبس الهمامة، وليس فيها علاه موضع يسير إليه ما انتزع منها؛ إذ غير هذا الجانب غير متناه، وهو بالتخلص يرجع إلى ما لا نهاية، فلا يجد لنفسه موضع قرار. فلا معنى للتخلص إلا أن تكون الظلمة تدفعه عن نفسها، فيكون دفعه خيرا، إذ كان حبسه شرا. مع ما إذا دفعت أجزاءه، وما علا ليس إلا أجزاؤه، فهو يدخل بعضه بعضا، وذلك نهاية. لكنه كانت تحبسه في جوهره ثم قهرت كلية النور فجعلته سجنا لنفسها تحبس فيه عدوها، فيصير عدوها بجوهره حبيسا لنفسه. وبعد، فإن الظلمة ليس لها في غير وجه الامتزاج حد، فهو إلى ما ذا يصير بالتخلص؟ فهو يبين أن لا معنى للتخلص. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
The extrication from it by substance is impossible, because it is not prevented from it by what necessitates the extrication of its parts from the imprisonment of al-hamama, and there is no place above it to which what is taken from it goes; since this side is not finite, and by extrication it returns to what has no end, so it finds no place of stability. So there is no meaning to extrication unless the darkness pushes it away from itself, then its pushing would be good, since its imprisonment was evil. Moreover, when it pushes its parts, and what is above is only its parts, so it enters some into others, and that is an end. But it used to imprison it in its substance, then the totality of light overpowered it, making it a prison for itself in which it imprisons its enemy, so its enemy becomes by its substance imprisoned to itself. Furthermore, darkness has no limit except in the aspect of mixture, so to what would it become by extrication? So it shows that there is no meaning to extrication. And there is no power except through Allah.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Manichaean idea that light can be extracted from darkness. Maturidi argues that since darkness is infinite (غير متناه), light has no place to go. Even if darkness pushed light away, that would be a good act from darkness, which contradicts its nature. Moreover, if light parts are pushed, they merely intermix again, leading to an end. The argument concludes that extrication is meaningless. The teacher should note that Maturidi uses logical reasoning to show the incoherence of dualist cosmology.

Key Terms
التخلص
الجوهر
الظلمة
النور
غير متناه
الهمامة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Maturidi is accepting the Manichaean dualist framework.
Correction: Maturidi uses the dualist premises to demonstrate their logical incoherence, not to endorse them.

Checkpoint
Why does Maturidi argue that extrication of light from darkness is impossible?
A) Because light is too weak to move.
B) Because darkness is infinite, leaving no place for light to go.
C) Because darkness would prevent it by force.
D) Because light is not a substance.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi refutes Manichaean dualism by showing that the concept of light being extracted from an infinite darkness is logically impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider the 'darkness' in your own life—whether it is sin, ignorance, or despair—do you ever fall into the illusion that you can escape it simply by moving to a different 'location' or situation? What does this lesson teach you about the futility of such a strategy?
?
If infinite darkness cannot be escaped by its own nature, what does that imply about your absolute need for a source of light that is not created or finite? Are you truly relying on that infinite Light, or are you still relying on your own efforts?
?
Maturidi shows that darkness pushing light would be a contradiction. Have you ever tried to justify evil by thinking it could produce good in your life? Confront that thought: in what areas are you rationalizing darkness as a means to light?

The Imprisoned Light Cannot Be the Source of Good
Maturidi questions how imprisoned light can be the source of good.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi argues that an imprisoned, powerless light cannot be the source of all good in the world.

Core Idea
Good cannot originate from a source that is itself powerless and imprisoned.

The Manichaeans claimed that all good comes from the substance of light, yet they also believed that light is imprisoned and overpowered by darkness. Maturidi exposes the absurdity: how can good arise from something that lacks power and freedom? This lesson unpacks that contradiction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the rhetorical questions Maturidi uses to highlight the inconsistency.
The tone is one of surprise (العجب).
2
Identify the core contradiction
Maturidi points out that if light is imprisoned and all action comes from darkness, then light cannot be a source of good. Find the phrases that show light's powerlessness.
3
Consider Maturidi's counterexample
He asks: unless light's parts that didn't rebel cast others into darkness – but that would be evil, not good. Understand this logical move.
This refutes any attempt to salvage good from light.
4
Reflect on the lesson's core idea
The key takeaway is that attributing good to a powerless source is contradictory. Think about how this applies to theological arguments.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشيخ رحمه الله: ثم العجب من قولهم إن الخير كله في العالم من جوهر النور؛ فمن أين يكون منه الخير وهو المقهور المحبوس؟ والفعل كله من الآخر ليحبسه به، فليس من النور غير البقاء في سجن الآخر ووثاقه، فمن أين يجيئ منه خير؟ إلا أن يرى ذلك سائر الأجزاء التي لم تبغ عليه، فيلقى أجزاءه في حبس أجزاء آخر، وذلك هو الشر؛ وأنى لملك الخير، وهو كله في الخلاص، وهو غير ممنوع. ثم التناقض أنهم جعلوا التباين بالجوهر فمحال امتزاجهما وهما بالجوهر متباينان وذلك قائم بحاله؛ إذ هم لا يرون الامتزاج غيرًا. على أنه يقال لهم: الامتزاج أليس كان بعد أن لم يكن؟ لا بد من «بلى». قيل: أكان هو النور أو الظلمة أو غيرهما؟ فإن قال بالأولين أحال، لأنه أثبت الامتزاج والتباين لنفسه؛ ولو جاز ذلك لجاز وجودهما معا، وهو بين. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
Then the sheikh (may Allah have mercy on him) said: Then it is surprising from their statement that all good in the world is from the substance of light; so from where would good come from it while it is the overpowered imprisoned? And all action is from the other to imprison it by it, so there is nothing from light except staying in the prison and chains of the other, so from where does good come from it? Unless it sees that the other parts that did not rebel against it, it casts its parts into the imprisonment of other parts, and that is evil. And how can it be the king of good, while it is entirely in liberation, and it is not prevented? Then the contradiction: they made distinctness by substance, so their mixture is impossible while they are distinct by substance, and that is established in its state; since they do not see mixture as other. Then it is said to them: Is the mixture created after it was not? There must be 'yes'. It is said: Was it the light or the darkness or something else? If he says the first two, he makes it impossible, because he affirms mixture and distinctness for itself; and if that were permissible, their existence together would be permissible, and that is clear. And there is no power except through Allah.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage presents two refutations. First, if light is the source of all good but is itself imprisoned and powerless, good cannot come from it; the only action is from darkness. Second, they claim light and darkness are essentially distinct (متباينان بالجوهر), yet they admit mixture; this is contradictory. They must answer whether the mixture is created or not; if created, what caused it? If they say light or darkness, that would attribute change to the eternal. Maturidi exposes the logical inconsistencies in the dualist system.

Key Terms
الخير
المقهور المحبوس
جوهر النور

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that good and evil can come from the same source, or that powerlessness doesn't prevent being a source of good.
Correction: Maturidi shows that if a source is powerless, it cannot produce good effects; good requires power and freedom.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, why is it contradictory for the Manichaeans to say that all good is from light while also claiming light is imprisoned?
A) Because light is not a substance.
B) Because imprisonment implies powerlessness, so good cannot come from a powerless source.
C) Because darkness is the source of good.
D) Because light and darkness are the same.

Key Takeaway
A source of good must be powerful and free; an imprisoned light cannot produce good.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that a source of good must be powerful and free. Where in your life are you depending on a 'light' that is actually weak or imprisoned—something or someone that cannot truly provide the good you seek? What will you do this week to shift your reliance to the All-Powerful Source?
?
Maturidi expresses surprise (العجب) at the inconsistency of the dualists. Is there any belief you hold that, upon honest examination, contradicts your actions or other beliefs? Will you commit to one hour this week to identifying and resolving such an inconsistency?
?
The light in this passage is described as 'entirely in liberation' yet unable to free itself. Are there areas in your soul where you feel trapped, constantly seeking freedom yet unable to break free? What step can you take today to turn to the One who is truly powerful to grant you liberation?

The Contradiction of Essential Distinctness and Mixture
Maturidi exposes the logical contradiction in dualist claims of distinctness and mixture.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi finds it contradictory for dualists to claim that light and darkness are essentially distinct while also allowing their mixture.

Core Idea
Things that are essentially distinct cannot mix—admitting mixture undermines their claimed distinctness.

The Manichaeans held that light and darkness are fundamentally different in substance (جوهر), yet they also believed these two substances can mix. Maturidi points out that this is logically impossible: if two things are essentially distinct, they cannot combine. He then presses the dualists with a further question: if mixture occurs, what is its origin? This lesson explores that logical trap.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the two parts: the contradiction itself, and the logical question about the origin of mixture.
The word 'التناقض' signals the main point.
2
Understand the contradiction
The dualists say light and darkness are متباينان بالجوهر (essentially distinct). If so, their mixture is impossible. Yet they affirm mixture. Why is that a contradiction?
Essential distinctness precludes any real union.
3
Examine Maturidi's question
He asks: 'Is the mixture created after it was not?' They must answer yes. Then 'Is it light, darkness, or something else?' If they say light or darkness, they attribute change to an eternal substance, which is impossible.
This forces them into a dilemma.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
If mixture were allowed for distinct substances, then light and darkness could coexist without mixture—which is also problematic. See how Maturidi closes the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشيخ رحمه الله: ثم العجب من قولهم إن الخير كله في العالم من جوهر النور؛ فمن أين يكون منه الخير وهو المقهور المحبوس؟ والفعل كله من الآخر ليحبسه به، فليس من النور غير البقاء في سجن الآخر ووثاقه، فمن أين يجيئ منه خير؟ إلا أن يرى ذلك سائر الأجزاء التي لم تبغ عليه، فيلقى أجزاءه في حبس أجزاء آخر، وذلك هو الشر؛ وأنى لملك الخير، وهو كله في الخلاص، وهو غير ممنوع. ثم التناقض أنهم جعلوا التباين بالجوهر فمحال امتزاجهما وهما بالجوهر متباينان وذلك قائم بحاله؛ إذ هم لا يرون الامتزاج غيرًا. على أنه يقال لهم: الامتزاج أليس كان بعد أن لم يكن؟ لا بد من «بلى». قيل: أكان هو النور أو الظلمة أو غيرهما؟ فإن قال بالأولين أحال، لأنه أثبت الامتزاج والتباين لنفسه؛ ولو جاز ذلك لجاز وجودهما معا، وهو بين. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
Then the sheikh (may Allah have mercy on him) said: Then it is surprising from their statement that all good in the world is from the substance of light; so from where would good come from it while it is the overpowered imprisoned? And all action is from the other to imprison it by it, so there is nothing from light except staying in the prison and chains of the other, so from where does good come from it? Unless it sees that the other parts that did not rebel against it, it casts its parts into the imprisonment of other parts, and that is evil. And how can it be the king of good, while it is entirely in liberation, and it is not prevented? Then the contradiction: they made distinctness by substance, so their mixture is impossible while they are distinct by substance, and that is established in its state; since they do not see mixture as other. Then it is said to them: Is the mixture created after it was not? There must be 'yes'. It is said: Was it the light or the darkness or something else? If he says the first two, he makes it impossible, because he affirms mixture and distinctness for itself; and if that were permissible, their existence together would be permissible, and that is clear. And there is no power except through Allah.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage presents two refutations. First, if light is the source of all good but is itself imprisoned and powerless, good cannot come from it; the only action is from darkness. Second, they claim light and darkness are essentially distinct (متباينان بالجوهر), yet they admit mixture; this is contradictory. They must answer whether the mixture is created or not; if created, what caused it? If they say light or darkness, that would attribute change to the eternal. Maturidi exposes the logical inconsistencies in the dualist system.

Key Terms
التباين
الامتزاج
جوهر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that two essentially different things can mix without changing their essential nature.
Correction: If two things are essentially distinct, they cannot mix; mixture would require a shared essence or a new category.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the main contradiction in the dualist position on light and darkness?
A) They claim light is good and darkness is evil.
B) They claim the substances are distinct yet they mix.
C) They claim both substances are eternal.
D) They claim mixture is evil.

Key Takeaway
Essential distinctness precludes mixture; claiming both is logically contradictory.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are there beliefs you hold about Allah that you have never logically examined, perhaps because they seem comforting or familiar? What would it mean for you to test them with the same rigor Maturidi applies here?
?
When you catch yourself holding two inconsistent ideas—about God, about yourself, or about others—what is your immediate reaction? Do you ignore the tension, or do you pursue consistency? How might this lesson change your approach?
?
The dualists clung to both distinctness and mixture because both seemed necessary to them. Is there any area in your life where you cling to two incompatible claims because letting go of either feels too costly? Can you, right now, identify a contradiction you need to resolve?
